|-
|}
In Demo mode, only the Scenario tab is accessible in the Launchpad dialog, to prevent users from modifying simulation configuration features such as screen resolution or plug-in modules. SpaceXpanse should be configured as required before launching into demo mode.

To use the auto-launch feature in demo mode, a folder Demo must be created in the main scenario folder. SpaceXpanse randomly picks a scenario from this folder to launch.

Note: When using SpaceXpanse in Demo mode, it is recommended that the simulation is run in a window, or in a fullscreen mode that matches the native screen resolution, to avoid excessive switching between video display modes.

= {{anchor|RefHeadingToc77683308146368}} Command line interface =

When starting SpaceXpanse (SpaceXpanse.exe) or the SpaceXpanse graphics server (SpaceXpanse_ng.exe) from the command line, optional parameters can be provided to modify the behaviour of the simulation.

SpaceXpanse.exe [options]

Below is a list of the supported options. Options are separated with space. Most options can be specified with a long notation (with prefix <tt>--</tt>) or short notation (with prefix <tt>-</tt>). If the option requires an argument, it must be separated from the option key with <tt><nowiki>=</nowiki></tt> (for the long version) or with a space (for the short version). If an argument contains spaces, it should be enclosed in double quotes (<tt>“</tt>).


{| style="border-spacing:0;margin:auto;width:5.7722in;"
|-
| style="background-color:#666666;border-top:0.05pt solid #000000;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding-top:0in;padding-bottom:0in;padding-left:0.0396in;padding-right:0.0396in;" | <span style="color:#ffffff;">Long</span>
| style="background-color:#666666;border-top:0.05pt solid #000000;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding-top:0in;padding-bottom:0in;padding-left:0.0396in;padding-right:0.0396in;color:#ffffff;" | Short
| style="background-color:#666666;border:0.05pt solid #000000;padding-top:0in;padding-bottom:0in;padding-left:0.0396in;padding-right:0.0396in;color:#ffffff;" | Effect
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | --help
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | <tt>-h</tt>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Display usage and list of options, then exit.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | --fastexit
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | -x
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Terminate SpaceXpanse at the end of the session. Don’t return to the Launchpad dialog.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | --scenario=<scn>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | <tt>-S <scn></tt>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Directly launch scenario <tt><scn></tt>. Bypass the Launchpad dialog. <tt><scn></tt> should contain the path to the scenario file relative to <tt>.\Scenarios</tt>. The file extension (<tt>.scn</tt>) should be omitted.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | --scenariox=<scn>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | -s <scn>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Shortcut for <tt>-x -S <scn></tt>. Launch scenario directly and terminate on session end.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | --openvideotab
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | -v
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Open Launchpad dialog on video tab instead of scenarios.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | --keeplog
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | -l
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Append log output to SpaceXpanse.log instead of overwriting the previous log data.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | --fixedstep=<s>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | -f <s>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Set a fixed simulation time step of <tt><s></tt> seconds for each frame, independent of how long the frame takes to render in real time.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | --maxsystime=<t>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | -T <t>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Terminate the simulation session after <tt><t></tt> seconds.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | --maxsimtime=<t>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | -t <t>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Terminate the simulation session at simulation time <tt><t></tt>.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | --maxframes=<f>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | 
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Terminate the simulation session after <tt><f></tt> time frames.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | --plugin=<pg>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | -p <pg>
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Enforce loading of plugin <tt><pg></tt>. Any path provided must be relative to <tt>.\Modules\Plugin</tt>. The extension (<tt>.dll</tt>) should be omitted. Multiple <tt>–plugin</tt> options can be provided. Any plug-ins requested on the command line cannot be unloaded interactively.


|-
|}
= {{anchor|RefHeadingToc175212151075092}} Glossary =

A list of technical terms and abbreviations frequently used in this manual and elsewhere in SpaceXpanse.


{| style="border-spacing:0;width:5.7674in;"
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:0.05pt solid #000000;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Albedo
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:0.05pt solid #000000;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Fraction of incident radiation reflected back diffusely by a body.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Apoapsis
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The point of an elliptic orbit farthest from the focus (from the orbited body). Body-specific names are sometimes used, e.g. ''apogee'' (for Earth orbits) or ''aphelion'' (for solar orbits). Orbital velocity is lowest at apoapsis. See also ''periapsis''.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Argument of periapsis
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The angle from ''ascending node'' to ''periapsis'' of an orbit, measured in the direction of motion (''ω''). One of the 6 primary 2-body orbital elements (defines the orientation of the orbit in the orbital plane).
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Ascending node
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | One of the points (nodes) of an orbit intersecting an inclined reference plane (e.g. the equator). At the ascending node, the orbiting object crosses the reference plane from south to north. See also ''descending node''.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Astronomical unit
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | One astronomical unit (1 AU) is the mean radius of Earth’s orbit around the sun (approximately 150 · 106 km). It is commonly used as a distance measure on interplanetary scales within the solar system.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Axial precession
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | A change in the orientation of the rotation axis of a rotating body (e.g. a planet). For example, Earth’s axis is precessing around the ecliptic pole at an angle of 23.5° over a period of 26000 years.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Delta-V
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Δv: The magnitude of a velocity change, specifically, a change of a spacecraft’s velocity, effected by engaging its engines to alter its trajectory. The amount of available Δv (''delta-v budget'') is limited by the remaining propellant (via the ''rocket equation''). Fuel is a limited resource, meaning that Δv requirements are an important aspect of mission planning.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Descending node
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | One of the points (nodes) of an orbit intersecting an inclined reference plane (e.g. the equator). At the descending node, the orbiting object crosses the reference plane from north to south. See also ''ascending node''.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Eccentricity
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Shape parameter for conic sections, e.g. 2-body orbits (''e''). Circular: ''e'' = 0, elliptic: 0 < ''e'' < 1, parabolic: ''e'' = 1, hyperbolic: ''e'' > 1. One of the 6 primary 2-body orbital elements.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Ecliptic
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The ecliptic is the Earth’s mean orbital plane. The orbital planes of most planetary bodies are close to the ecliptic, which makes it an important reference plane for interplanetary missions. The ecliptic undergoes slight variations over time due to gravitational perturbations, so a reference date (epoch), e.g. J2000.0 must be added to define a fixed plane.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Geostationary orbit
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | A circular equatorial orbit with an orbit period equal to the orbited body’s sidereal rotation period. As a result, the orbiting object maintains its position above a point on the equator, at zero ground speed. For Earth, geostationary orbits are at an altitude of ~36000 km. Geostationary orbits are often used by communication or weather satellites.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | HUD
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Head-up display. Avionics display used in modern aircraft and spacecraft that projects data and visual cues onto a transparent screen directly in the pilot’s line of sight.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | IDS
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Instrument docking system. A fictional universal docking system that provides linear and rotational alignment cues for docking approaches, similar to ILS.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | ILS
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Instrument Landing System. A combination of radio transmitters installed at a runway, and onboard receivers and avionics displays to provide an aircraft pilot with deviation cues from a target approach path. In SpaceXpanse, this is also used by horizontally landing spacecraft, including a (fictional) ILS at the Kennedy SLF.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Inclination
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The angle between the orbital plane and a reference plane (''i''). One of the 6 primary orbital elements to describe a 2-body orbit (defines the orientation of the orbital plane in space together with the ''longitude of the ascending node'').
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Inertia tensor
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | A 3x3 matrix that defines a rigid body’s resistance to a change of its angular velocity around its axes, analogous to the role of mass in linear kinematics:

L = Iω (L: angular momentum, I: inertia tensor, ω: angular velocity)
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Isp
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Specific impulse (''I''<sub>sp</sub>). Equivalent to effective exhaust velocity ''v''<sub>e</sub> [m/s]. Specifies the amount of thrust [N] produced by burning propellant at a rate of 1 kg/s. An often used alternative definition for ''I''<sub>sp</sub> is ''v''<sub>e</sub> · ''g''<sub>0</sub> [s] with standard gravity ''g''<sub>0</sub> <nowiki>=</nowiki> 9.81 m/s<sup>2</sup>.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | LEO
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Low Earth orbit. An orbit with an an apogee altitude of less than ~2000 km and an orbital period of less than ~128 minutes. Objects in LEO can experience orbit degradation due to atmospheric friction, limiting their lifetime unless periodically boosted to compensate, such as the ISS.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Line of nodes
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The intersection of the orbital plane with an inclined reference plane. Contains the ''ascending'' and ''descending nodes''.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Longitude of the ascending node
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The angle in the reference plane between reference direction (e.g. vernal point) and the orbit’s ascending node (''Ω''). One of the primary 2-body orbital elements (defines the orientation of the orbital plane in space together with ''inclination'').
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Mean anomaly
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Fraction of orbital period passed since apoapsis passage, expressed as an angle (''M''). Equivalent to true anomaly of a fictitious circular orbit with the same orbital period as the actual orbit. Unlike true anomaly in a non-circular orbit, mean anomaly varies linearly with time.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Mean longitude
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The sum of ''longitude of the ascending node'', ''argument of periapsis'' and ''mean anomaly'': ''l ''<nowiki>= </nowiki>''Ω'' + ''ω'' + ''M''. See also ''true longitude''.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | MET
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Mission elapsed time. A time scale for mission events referenced to launch time. 
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | MFD
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Multifunctional display. An avionics instrument consisting of a digital display and input device. Can display a variety of data and combines multiple traditional aircraft/spacecraft instruments.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Normal
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The direction perpendicular to a plane. In orbital operations, attitudes normal to the orbital plane are often used for out-of-plane manoeuvres, such as plane rotations. SpaceXpanse differentiates between normal (in the direction of the momentum vector '''r''' x '''v''') and anti-normal (in the opposite direction). See also ''specific relative angular momentum''.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Orbital elements
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | 6 scalar values defining the Keplerian (2-body) orbital motion of an object in the unperturbed field of a gravitational point source. Shape and size of the orbit are defined by semi-major axis (''a'') and eccentricity (''e''); orientation of the orbital plane is defined by inclination (''i'') and longitude of the ascending node (''Ω''); orientation of the orbit in the plane is defined by argument of periapsis (''ω''); position of the orbiting object along the orbit is given by true anomaly (''ν'') at a given time. See also ''state vectors''.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Osculating elements
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The momentary ''orbital elements'' of a body corresponding to its current ''state vectors''. In the presence of gravitational forces in addition to the primary, the orbit is perturbed and the osculating elements change over time.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Patched conic approximation
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Approximate trajectory calculation in the presence of multiple gravitational sources. The trajectory is constructed from partial conic sections, assuming only a single source for each section within the ''sphere of influence'' of that body. The sections are joined by continuity conditions for the state vectors.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Periapsis
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The point of an elliptic orbit closest to the focus (the orbited body). Body-specific names are sometimes used, e.g. perigee (for Earth orbits) or perihelion (for solar orbits). Orbital velocity is highest at periapsis. See also ''apoapsis''.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | PMI
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Principal moments of inertia: the diagonal elements of the ''inertia tensor'' expressed in the principal body frame where the inertia tensor is diagonal. See Technotes/composite.pdf for more details.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Prograde
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The ''prograde direction'' of an orbiting body is that of the current orbital velocity vector. In a ''prograde orbit'' the orbiting body is moving in the direction of the rotation of the orbited body. See also ''retrograde''.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | RCS
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Reaction Control System. A set of thrusters on a spacecraft that provides attitude control. Usually engaged in pairs to create angular moments (in angular mode) or linear moments (in linear mode) in the 3 main spacecraft axes.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Retrograde
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The ''retrograde direction'' of an orbiting body is the direction opposite to the current orbital velocity vector. In a ''retrograde orbit'' the orbiting body is moving in the opposite direction to the rotation of the orbited body. See also ''prograde''.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Semi-major axis
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Longest half-axis of an ellipse (''a''). One of the 6 primary 2-body orbital elements (defines the shape of the orbit together with the ''eccentricity'').
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Semi-minor axis
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Shortest half-axis of an ellipse.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Sidereal day
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Time for one full (360°) rotation of a celestial body. Used in astronomy, where a star will appear at the same position in the sky at the same sidereal time. Shorter than a ''synodic day'', which also has to take into account the apparent motion of the sun in front of the celestial background, caused by the planet’s orbital motion.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | SOI
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Sphere of influence: region around a planet or moon where the gravitational influence on an object is predominantly caused by that body. Used for approximate trajectory calculations (''patched conic approximation''), where the SOI surfaces define the endpoints of the conic sections.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Specific relative angular momentum
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The vector product of an orbiting object’s position and velocity vectors: '''h''' = '''r''' x '''v'''. '''h''' is normal (perpendicular) to the orbital plane.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | SRB
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Solid rocket booster. Solid propellant rocket used to provide additional thrust during first stage ascent of a launch vehicle, in particular the Space Shuttle.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | State vectors
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Cartesian position ('''r''') and velocity ('''v''') vectors of an orbiting body at a given time. Uniquely defines an unperturbed (Keplerian) orbit. From the state vectors, the 6 orbital elements of the corresponding 2-body orbit can be calculated, and vice versa.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | Synodic day
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Mean period between two meridian passages of the sun, averaged over a year. For a planet rotating prograde, this requires a rotation > 360° to account for the orbital movement of the planet around its sun, and is therefore longer than a ''sidereal day''. The length of a synodic day varies annually on a planet with an elliptic orbit.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | True anomaly
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Angular distance of an orbital position from periapsis, as measured from the focus (''ν'').
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | True longitude
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | The sum of ''longitude of the ascending node'', ''argument of periapsis'' and ''true anomaly'': ''L ''<nowiki>= </nowiki>''Ω'' + ''ω'' + ''ν)''. See also ''mean longitude''.
|-
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:0.05pt solid #000000;border-right:none;padding:0.0396in;" | VTOL
| style="background-color:#f2f2f2;border-top:none;border-bottom:0.05pt solid #000000;border-left:none;border-right:0.05pt solid #000000;padding:0.0396in;" | Vertical take-off and landing. Spacecraft can use downward directed engines to compensate for gravitational acceleration and enable vertical take-off and soft touchdown, either using main engines (“tailsitters”) or dedicated hover engines. Spacecraft with lifting bodies or airfoils may more efficiently use horizontal runway take-offs and/or landings on planets with sufficient atmospheric density.
